***zich.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:zich.html>zich</a> (176)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">sich</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_High_German" class="extiw" title="w:Middle High German">Middle High German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="gmh">sich</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_High_German" class="extiw" title="w:Old High German">Old High German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="goh">sih</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-West_Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-West Germanic language">Proto-West Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gmw-pro">*sik</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*sek</i>. Old Dutch did not have a reflexive pronoun (only rarely in early Limburgish texts), but used the normal accusative pronoun (if necessary intensified by <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">selven</i>, cf. English <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">himself</i>). Although the use of <i><a href = vnd.unilang:zich.html>zich</a></i> in Holland-based Dutch <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> clearly triggered by written German, this development <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> assisted by the fact that the south-eastern dialects of Dutch <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> already adopted certain High German pronoun forms in much earlier times (cf. Limburgish <i class="Latn mention" lang="li">ich</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="li">mich</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="li">dich</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="li"><a href = vnd.unilang:zich.html>zich</a></i>).
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pronoun_2">Pronoun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zich.html>zich</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">by extension<span class="ib-comma">,</span> reflexive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="use-with-mention">Third person singular and plural reflexive pronoun</span>; himself, herself, itself, themselves, oneself
<dl><dd><i><a href = vnd.unilang:hij.html>Hij</a> wast <b><a href = vnd.unilang:zich.html>zich</a></b>.</i>  |  He washes <b>himself</b>.</dd>
<dd><i><a href = vnd.unilang:hij.html>Hij</a> wast <b><a href = vnd.unilang:zich.html>zich</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:het.html>het</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:gezicht.html>gezicht</a>.</i>  |  He washes his face.</dd>
<dd><i>Ieder <a href = vnd.unilang:voor.html>voor</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:zich.html>zich</a></b>.</i>  |  Every <a href = vnd.unilang:man.html>man</a> for <b>himself</b>.</dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">by extension<span class="ib-comma">,</span> formal<span class="ib-comma">,</span> reflexive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="use-with-mention">Second person singular and plural formal reflexive pronoun</span>; yourself, yourselves
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl">Sloeg <a href = vnd.unilang:u.html>u</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:zich.html>zich</a></b> in <a href = vnd.unilang:het.html>het</a> donker?</i> ― <span class="e-translation">Did you hit <b>yourself</b> in the dark?</span></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:u.html>U</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:kunt.html>kunt</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:zich.html>zich</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:hier.html>hier</a> scheren.</i> ― <span class="e-translation">You can shave here.</span></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl">Vergist <a href = vnd.unilang:u.html>u</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:zich.html>zich</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:niet.html>niet</a>?</i> ― <span class="e-translation">Aren't you mistaken?</span></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="use-with-mention">expresses an unintended result with many otherwise non-reflexive and ergative verbs</span>
<dl><dd><i><a href = vnd.unilang:hij.html>Hij</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:vallen.html>viel</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:zich.html>zich</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:een.html>een</a> ongeluk</i>  |  He fell and this resulted in an accident.</dd>
<dd><i><a href = vnd.unilang:hij.html>Hij</a> lachte <b><a href = vnd.unilang:zich.html>zich</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:een.html>een</a> bult</i>  |  He laughed so severely that it left him a hunchback.</dd></dl></li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Usage_notes">Usage notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<ul><li><i><a href = vnd.unilang:zich.html>Zich</a></i> can be used whether the reflexivity of the verb <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> optional or mandatory. Optionally reflexive verbs can also take <i>zichzelf</i> as reflexive pronoun.</li>
<li>As in English (but unlike German and French), Dutch reflexive pronouns do not express reciprocity, except dialectally. Reciprocal senses may occur in fixed verb constructions, as in: <i><a href = vnd.unilang:ze.html>Ze</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:hebben.html>hebben</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:zich.html>zich</a></i> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">verloofd</i>. (“They have got engaged.”) Such cases are generally explainable by etymology. (In the example, the original sense <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> “They have promised themselves [to each other].”)</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Inflection">Inflection</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>

***zien.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:zien.html>zien</a> (94)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">sien</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">sian</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*sehwaną</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*sekʷ-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to see, notice</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Originally a class 5 strong verb, but the Germanic <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*h</i> <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> lost from the infinitive and present tense forms through syncope in Old Dutch. However, it alternated with <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*g</i> in the past tense through <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grammatischer_Wechsel" class="extiw" title="w:Grammatischer Wechsel">Grammatischer Wechsel</a>, and this remained.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zien.html>zien</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to see
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:ik.html>Ik</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:zie.html>zie</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:jouw.html>jouw</a> kat!</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">I <b>see</b> your cat!</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li></ol>

<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Persoonlijk_voornaamwoord"><i>Persoonlijk voornaamwoord</i></span></h4> <p><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="cite_note-2"> | 2 | </a></sup>
</p><ol><li>3e persoon enkelvoud vrouwelijk, <i>nominatief</i>
<dl><dd><ul><li><i><a href = vnd.unilang:heeft.html>Heeft</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:zij.html>zij</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:dat.html>dat</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:gezegd.html>gezegd</a> of <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:het.html>het</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:haar.html>haar</a> echtgenoot?</i> </li></ul></dd></dl></li>
<li>3e persoon meervoud, <i>nominatief</i>
<dl><dd><ul><li><i><a href = vnd.unilang:hebben.html>Hebben</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:zij.html>zij</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:dat.html>dat</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:gedaan.html>gedaan</a> of <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:het.html>het</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>de</a> oppositie?</i> </li></ul></dd></dl></li></ol>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Synoniemen"><i>Synoniemen</i></span></h5>

***zijn.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:zijn.html>zijn</a> (20)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">sijn</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">sīn</i>. The infinitive <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zijn.html>zijn</a></i> along with the words <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a></i> and <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zij.html>zij</a></i> (present indicative and subjunctive) derive ultimately from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*h₁es-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to be</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, which <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> no separate infinitive in Germanic. The modern infinitive <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> probably back-formed in late Old Dutch from the first-person plural subjunctive <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">sīn</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss"><a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a> be</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, since this form <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> become identical to the infinitive in other verbs during the late Old Dutch period. Compare also <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">sein</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Low_German" class="extiw" title="w:Low German">Low German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nds">sien</i>.
</p><p>The original infinitive survives in <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:wees.html>wezen</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">wesen</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">wesan</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*wesaną</i>, from <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*h₂wes-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to reside</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. All the forms with initial <i>w-</i> (imperative and past tense) derive from this root.
</p><p>Finally, the forms <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:ben.html>ben</a></i> and <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:bent.html>bent</a></i> derive from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*beuną</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to be, to become</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*BʰuH-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to become</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, which survives only as relic forms in the West Germanic languages and not at all in the others. Its infinitive and non-singular forms are only attested in (Old) English.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zijn.html>zijn</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To be, to exist.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><b><a href = vnd.unilang:zijn.html>Zijn</a></b> of <a href = vnd.unilang:niet.html>niet</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:zijn.html>zijn</a></b>, <a href = vnd.unilang:dat.html>dat</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>de</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:vraag.html>vraag</a>.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">To <b>be</b> or not to <b>be</b>, that <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> the question.</span></dd></dl></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><b><a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>Was</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:je.html>je</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:er.html>er</a> afgelopen zaterdag <a href = vnd.unilang:ook.html>ook</a>?</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation"><b>Were</b> you there too last Saturday?</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive<span class="ib-comma">,</span> copulative</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="use-with-mention">Used to connect a noun to an adjective that describes it.</span>
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>De</a> bal <b><a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a></b> rond.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">The ball <b><a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a></b> round.</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive<span class="ib-comma">,</span> auxiliary</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="use-with-mention">Used to form the perfect tense of the active voice of some verbs, together with a past participle.<br /><b>Note:</b> The perfect tense of most other verbs <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> formed using <a href = vnd.unilang:hebben.html>hebben</a>.</span>
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:hij.html>Hij</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:hier.html>hier</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:geweest.html>geweest</a>.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">He <b>has</b> been here.</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive<span class="ib-comma">,</span> auxiliary</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="use-with-mention">Used to form the perfect tense of the passive voice, together with a past participle.<br /><b>Note:</b> The imperfect tense passive <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> formed using <a href = vnd.unilang:worden.html>worden</a>.</span>
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:ze.html>Ze</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:waren.html>waren</a></b> gered.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">They <b><a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> been</b> saved.</span></dd></dl></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>De</a> muur <b><a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a></b> geschilderd.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">The wall <b>has been</b> painted.</span></dd></dl></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>De</a> muur <a href = vnd.unilang:zal.html>zal</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:zijn.html>zijn</a></b> geschilderd.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">The wall will <b>have been</b> painted.</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive<span class="ib-comma">,</span> auxiliary</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="use-with-mention">Used to form the continuous forms of various tenses, together with <b><a href = vnd.unilang:aan.html>aan</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:het.html>het</a></b> or, in archaic style, with a present participle.</span>
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>De</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:man.html>man</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:aan.html>aan</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:het.html>het</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:lopen.html>lopen</a>.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">The <a href = vnd.unilang:man.html>man</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a></b> walking.</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To go, to go on a trip and return.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:ik.html>Ik</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:ben.html>ben</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:even.html>even</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:naar.html>naar</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>de</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:dokter.html>dokter</a>.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">I <b>am going</b> to the doctor for a while.</span></dd></dl></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:ik.html>Ik</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:ben.html>ben</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:vandaag.html>vandaag</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:naar.html>naar</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:het.html>het</a> strand <b><a href = vnd.unilang:geweest.html>geweest</a>.</b></i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">I've <b>been</b> to the beach today.</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive<span class="ib-comma">,</span> impersonal</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="use-with-mention">Used to indicate weather, temperature or some other general condition.</span>
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:het.html>Het</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:erg.html>erg</a> warm <a href = vnd.unilang:vandaag.html>vandaag</a>.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">It <b><a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a></b> very warm today.</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive<span class="ib-comma">,</span> copulative<span class="ib-comma">,</span> mathematics</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to be, to equal, to total, to amount to; <span class="use-with-mention">used to indicate that the values on either side of an equation are the same.</span>
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:drie.html>Drie</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:keer.html>keer</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:vijf.html>vijf</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a></b> vijftien.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">Three times five <b><a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a></b> fifteen.</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li></ol>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Inflection">Inflection</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h5>
<ul><li>Generally, the infinitive <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:wees.html>wezen</a></i>, the present participle <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">wezend</i> and the present subjunctive <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">weze</i> and <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:wees.html>wezen</a></i> are also used. While the subjunctive <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> considered archaic, it persists in some fixed expressions such as <i><a href = vnd.unilang:als.html>als</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:zijn.html>ware</a></i> ("as if [it] were").</li>
<li><i><a href = vnd.unilang:zijn.html>Zijn</a></i> has special forms for the pronominal imperatives of <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:u.html>u</a></i> and <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:jullie.html>jullie</a></i>. Thus, <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zijn.html>weest</a></i> <i><a href = vnd.unilang:u.html>u</a>!</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:wees.html>wezen</a></i> <i><a href = vnd.unilang:jullie.html>jullie</a>!</i>, rather than the regular <i><a href = vnd.unilang:bent.html>bent</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:u.html>u</a>!, <a href = vnd.unilang:zijn.html>zijn</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:jullie.html>jullie</a>!</i>, which are less common. The simple imperative <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:wees.html>wees</a></i> in all cases. In Belgium the singular imperative <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zij.html>zij</a></i> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> also used.</li></ul>

<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h5>
<ul><li><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">archaic in standard Dutch</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span> <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:wees.html>wezen</a></span></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">obsolete in standard Dutch</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span> <span class="Latn" lang="nl">bennen</span></li></ul>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Derived_terms">Derived terms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h5>
<ul><li><span class="Latn" lang="nl">voorzijn</span></li>
<li><span class="Latn" lang="nl">welzijn</span></li></ul>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">sijn</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">sīn</i> (originally a reflexive form), from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*sīnaz</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*seyno-</i>. Cognate with <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">sein</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swedish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Swedish language">Swedish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="sv">sin</i>. Ultimately a form of the Proto-Indo-European reflexive pronoun <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*swe</i>, related to Russian <i class="Cyrl mention" lang="ru">себя</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="ru-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">sebja</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, Latin <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">suus</i>, Ancient Greek <i class="polytonic mention" lang="grc">ἑός</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="grc-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">heós</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> etc.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Determiner">Determiner</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zijn.html>zijn</a></strong> (<i>dependent possessive, independent possessive</i> <b class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zijn.html>zijne</a></b>, <i>contracted form</i> <b class="Latn" lang="nl">z'n</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>Third-person singular, masculine and neuter possessive pronoun: his, its.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:een.html>Een</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:man.html>man</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:en.html>en</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:zijn.html>zijn</a></b> hond.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">A <a href = vnd.unilang:man.html>man</a> and <b>his</b> dog.</span></dd></dl></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:een.html>Een</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:man.html>man</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:en.html>en</a> <b>z'n</b> hoed.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">A <a href = vnd.unilang:man.html>man</a> and <b>his</b> hat.</span></dd></dl></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:een.html>Een</a> boek <a href = vnd.unilang:en.html>en</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:zijn.html>zijn</a></b> kaft.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">A book and <b>its</b> cover.</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li></ol>

***zitten.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:zitten.html>zitten</a> (168)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">sitten</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">sitten</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*sitjaną</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*sed-</i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zitten.html>zitten</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to sit</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to be, to be placed or located
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:ik.html>Ik</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:zit.html>zit</a></b> in <a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>de</a> trein.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">I <b>am</b> on the train.</span></dd><dd>(literally, “<span class="e-literally">I <b>sit</b> in the train.</span>”)</dd></dl></div></dd>
<dd><span class="nyms synonym"><span class="defdate">Synonyms:</span> <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:liggen.html>liggen</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:lopen.html>lopen</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:staan.html>staan</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zijn.html>zijn</a></span></span></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">auxiliary<span class="ib-comma">,</span> with <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:te.html>te</a></i></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="use-with-mention">Forms a continuous aspect. Although it carries an implication of sitting, this <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> vague and <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> not strictly required or emphasized.</span>

<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">sōne</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">suno</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*sunuz</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*SuHnús</i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_2">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zoon.html>zoon</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zoon.html>zoons</a></b> <i>or</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl">zonen</b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zoon.html>zoontje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li>son
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:mijn.html>Mijn</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:zoon.html>zoon</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:wil.html>wil</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:met.html>met</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>de</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:zijn.html>jouwe</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:spelen.html>spelen</a>.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">My <b>son</b> wants to play with yours.</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li></ol>

***zorg.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:zorg.html>zorg</a> (443)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">sorge</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">sorghe</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">surghe</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">*sworga</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">*sorga</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*surgō</i>, ultimately from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*swergʰ-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">watch <a href = vnd.unilang:over.html>over</a>, worry; be ill, suffer</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Compare <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">Sorge</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Frisian_language" class="extiw" title="w:West Frisian language">West Frisian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fy">soarch</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">sorrow</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Danish language">Danish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="da">sorg</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swedish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Swedish language">Swedish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="sv">sorg</i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>

</p>
<ol><li>care</li>
<li>concern, worry</li></ol>

<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">sorgen</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">sorgon</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*surgāną</i>. <head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:zullen.html>zullen</a> (189)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">solen</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">suelen</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">sollen</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">sullen</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">skulan</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">sulan</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*skulaną</i>. Compare <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">sollen</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">shall</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Danish language">Danish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="da">skulle</i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>

<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:dat.html>Dat</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:zou.html>zou</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:ik.html>ik</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:niet.html>niet</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:doen.html>doen</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:als.html>als</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:ik.html>ik</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:jou.html>jou</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a>.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">I <b>would</b> not do that if I were you.</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Inflection">Inflection</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Usage_notes">Usage notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p>Although there are two conjugated forms for the second person in the present, there <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> no preferred or more common form as both are used and understood universally throughout the Dutch speaking world. One or the other may be preferred only in certain regions.
</p>

***zult.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:zult.html>zult</a> (441)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zult.html>zult</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="use-with-mention">second-person singular present indicative of <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zullen.html>zullen</a></i></span></li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">sulte</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">brine, salted food</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">sulta</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">salt water</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*sultijō</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">salt water, brine</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. Cognate with <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Saxon" class="extiw" title="w:Old Saxon">Old Saxon</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="osx">sultia</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_High_German" class="extiw" title="w:Old High German">Old High German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="goh">sulza</i> (German <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">Sülze</i>).
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:zult.html>zult</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span> (<i>uncountable</i>)
</p>
<ol><li>brawn, head cheese</li></ol>
